PROPOSED ORDINANCE AMENDMENT

Submitting a Proposed Ordinance sponsored by
LARRY SUFFREDIN and FORREST CLAYPOOL, County Commissioners
PROPOSED ORDINANCE AMENDMENT
ORDINANCE AMENDING CHAPTER 10:
THE CONTRACT AND PURCHASING ORDINANCE OF COOK COUNTY
WHEREAS, Cook County is a home rule unit of local government pursuant to Article 7, Section 6a of
the Illinois Constitution of 1970 with power to regulate those matters which pertain to its government and
affairs; and
WHEREAS, in the exercise of home rule powers, Cook County adopted an ordinance governing
procurement authority for the offices and departments of Cook County Government.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED THAT:

Section I. I 0 43.8., eHrreAtly " Reser'ied," I 0-43.6 is amended to read as follows:
10 43.8 (M) BROKERS:

(])

No contractor under this Ordinance shall act as a "broker". "Broker" means a person or entity
that fills orders by purchasing or receiving supplies from a third party supplier rather than out of
its own existing inventory and provides no substantial seivice other than acting as a conduit
between his or her supplier and his or her customer.

Section 2. This amendatory ordinance shall take effect and be in force immediately after its passage.

Commissioner Suffredin, seconded by Commissioner Maldonado, moved that the Proposed Ordinance
Amendment, as amended be referred to the Committee on Contract Compliance. (Comm. No. 27 1497).
T he motion carried unanimously.

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 7, 2005

PROPOSED RESOLUTION

RESOLUTION AFFIRMING NATIONAL POLICY AGAINST TORTURE
WHEREAS, as elected officials of Cook County, Illinois, we have an obligation to uphold the laws that
govern Cook County, the State of Illinois, the Constitution of the United States of America and all
international treaties to which the United States is party, including the Geneva Conventions of 1949, the
International Covenant on Civil and Political Rights, the Convention Against Torture and other Cruel,
Inhuman or Degrading Treatment or Punishment and related standards of international human rights; and
WHEREAS, the use of torture and other cruel inhuman or degrading treatment upon any person under
the physical control of and inflicted by any federal authority, including civilian contractors, constitutes a
violation of the law of nations in that customary international law prohibits torture as reflected, expressed,
and defined in multilateral treaties and other international instruments, international and domestic judicial
decisions, and other authorities; and
WHEREAS, the use of torture and other cruel, inhuman or degrading treatment upon any person under
the physical control of and inflicted by any federal authority, including civilian contractors, constitutes a
violation of the United States Constitution. The acts of mistreatment aforementioned constitute a
violation of the Fifth Amendment and of the Eighth Amendment's prohibition on cruel and unusual
punishment; and
WHEREAS, the use of torture and other cruel, inhuman or degrading treatment upon any person under
the physical control of and inflicted by any federal authority, including civilian contractors, constitutes a
violation of specific protections afforded by the Third and Fourth Geneva Conventions, including but not
limited to, Article 3 common to all four Geneva Conventions. Violations of Common Article 3 of the
Geneva Conventions are treaty violations as well as violations of customary international law; and
WHEREAS, the use of torture and other cruel, inhuman or degrading treatment upon any person under
the physical control of and inflicted by any federal authority, including civilian contractors, constitutes a
violation of Articles 7 and 10 of the International Covenant on Civil and Political Rights (lCCPR).
Violations of these provisions are treaty violations as well as violations of customary international law;
and
WHEREAS, the use of torture and other cruel, inhuman or degrading treatment upon any person under
the physical control of and inflicted by any federal authority, including civilian contractors, constitutes a
violation of the Convention Against Torture and Other Cruel, Inhuman or Degrading Treatment or
Punishment (CAT), and where applicable also of the federal anti-torture statute, 18 U .S .C. Section 23402340A, which Congress enacted to fulfill U.S. obligations under CAT. Violations of CAT are treaty
violations as well as violations of customary international law; and
WHEREAS, the use of torture and other cruel, inhuman or degrading treatment as a method of extracting
intelligence infonnation may lead to inaccurate and misleading infonnation. The Army Field Manual on
Intelligence Interrogation states: "the use of torture and other illegal methods is a poor technique that
yields unreliable results, may damage subsequent collection efforts, and can induce the source to say what
he thinks the interrogator wants to hear"; and
\VHEREAS, the use of torture and other cruel, inhuman or degrading treatment upon a foreign national
in U.S. custody may have the effect of radicalizing the victim's own moderate political, social or religious
ideologies. The aforementioned acts of mistreatment may also have the effect of radicalizing the
ideologies of the society from where the victim originates. Radicalized ideologies may increase the threat
of terrorism against Americans; and

1719

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 7, 2005

WHEREAS, the use of torture and other cruel, inhuman or degrading treatment upon a foreign national
in U.S. custody may increase the likelihood that kidnapped or captured American citizens and military
personnel will be subjected to similar acts of mistreatment. The U.S. Anny Field Manual on Intelligence
and Interrogation states: "the use of torture and other illegal methods] may also place U.S. and allied
personnel in enemy hands at great risk of abuse by their captors"; and
WHEREAS, the use of torture and other cruel, inhuman or degrading treatment undennines the rule of
law and delegitimizes the United States government as an advocate for democracy. The U.S. Anny Field
Manual on Intelligence Interrogation states: " Revelation of use of torture by U.S. personnel will bring
discredit upon the U.S. and its anned forces while undermining domestic and international support for the
war effort"; and
WHEREAS, the U.S. Anny Field Manual on Intelligence and Interrogation states that binding
international treaties and U.S. policy "expressly prohibit acts of violence or intimidation, including
physical or mental torture, threats, insults, or exposure to inhuman treatment as a means of or aid to
interrogation. Such illegal acts are not authorized and will not be condoned by the U.S. Army." The
Manual specifically defines "physical torture" to include " infliction of pain through chem icals or
bondage", " forcing an individual to stand, sit or kneel in abnormal positions for prolong periods of time",
"food deprivation" and "any form of beating".
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that We, the Board of Commissioners of Cook County,
condemn the use of torture and all cruel, inhuman or degrading treatment upon any person under the
physical control of any federal authority, including civilian contractors; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that We, the Board of Commissioners of Cook County, call on the
President and Congress to affirm the domestic and international obligations of the United States of
America to the rule of law and end the use of torture and all other cruel, inhuman or degrading treatment
as a matter of policy and to condemn the aforementioned acts of mistreatment; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be sent to President George W.
Bush and the Members of the Illinois Congressional delegation representing Cook County and let it also
be spread upon the official proceedings of this Honorable Body.
Commissioner Suffredin, seconded by Commissioner Maldonado, moved that the Resolution be approved
and adopted.
Commissioner Silvestri asked leave to add the full name of the President to the final resolved clause.
Leave was granted.
Commissioner Peraica, second by Commissioner Hansen, moved to delete "and end the use of to11ure and
all other cruel inhuman or degrading treatment as a matter of policy" from the resolved clause. The
motion was withdrawn.
Following discussion, Commissioner Suffredin, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved that the
Proposed Resolution, as amended be referred to the Committee on Human Relations. The motion was
withdrawn.
Commissioner Suffredin, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved that the Proposed Resolution, as
amended be referred to the Committee on Finance. (Comm. No. 27 1498). The motion carried
unanimously.

Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by
ROBERT MALDONADO, County Commissioner
Co-Sponsored by
LARRY SUFFREDIN, County Commissioner
PROPOSED RESOLUTION

COOK COUNTY EQUAL EMPLOYMENT OPPORTUNITY PLAN
WHEREAS, the President of the Cook County Board of Commissioners has instituted the "Cook County
Equal Employment Opportun ity Plan" for offices under the President, and has appointed an Equal
Employment Opportunity Officer (EEOP officer) to promote equal employment opportunity principles
throughout the Cook County workforce; and
WHEREAS, in order to give such policy and procedure the full force of the County's lawmaking powers
and to ensure equal employment opportunities for persons from all segments of the County community
without regard to race, ethnicity, gender, sexual orientation or any other protected category established by
law, statute or ordinance, it is essential to codify the affirmative action policy and procedure of the
County; and
WHEREAS, according to the Equal Employment Opportunity Coord inating Council 's Policy Statement
on Affinnative Action, 41 C.F.R. ยง 60-3. 17, the first step in the establishment of an affirmative action
plan is an analysis of the employer's work force to detennine whether the percentages of persons within
race, ethnic, gender, or sexual orientation groups in individual job c lassifications are substantially similar
to the percentages of persons within those groups who are available in the relevant job market and who
possess the basic job-related qualifications; and
WHEREAS, if substantial disparities are found, the next step in the establishment of an affirmative
action program is to examine each element of the overall selection process to determine which elements
operate to exclude persons on the basis of race, ethnicity, gender, or sexual orientation, and also to
detennine the validity of the element in predicting job perfonnance; and
WHEREAS, a prel iminary statistical analysis known as the "Cook County Employee Diversity
Representation Report," demonstrates a striking disparity in minority hiring among many of Cook
County's public offices; and
WHEREAS, a more comprehensive analysis of the County' s work force is necessary to substantiate
these hiring disparities before codifying a Cook County affinnative action plan.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Chief of the Bureau of Human Resources and the
County' s EEOP officer are directed to prepare a four year retroactive analysis of the County's work force
to determine whether percentages of race, ethnic, gender, or sexual orientation groups in individual job
classifications are substantially similar to the percentages of those groups available in the relevant job
market who possess the basic job-related qualifications and to provide a report to the Board sixty days
subsequent to the enactment of this Resolution; and

1721

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 7, 2005

BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that if a substantial disparity is found through statistical analysis, the
Chief of the Bureau of Human Resources and the County's EEOP officer are furt her directed to examine
each element of the overall selection process to determine which elements operate to exclude persons on
the basis of race, ethnic, gender, or sexual orientation and also to determine the validity of the element in
predicting job performance; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the heads of departments and agencies under authority of the
President are directed to cooperate fully with the Chief of the Bureau of Human Resources and the
County's EEOP officer in their efforts to prepare these studies; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the separately Elected Officials of the County, including the
Assessor, the Chief Judge of the Circuit Court, the Clerk of the Circuit Court, the Commissioners of the Board
of Review, the County Clerk, the Recorder of Deeds, the Sheriff, the State's Attorney and the Treasurer are
directed to prepare similar studies for personnel directly employed within their offices and to provide a
report to the Board sixty days subsequent to the enactment of this Resolution.

Commissioner Silvestri , seconded by Commissioner Maldonado, moved to suspend the rules so that this
matter may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.
Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved that the Proposed Resolution be
referred to the Committee on Finance. (Comm. No. 27 1503). The motion carried unanimously.

* * * * *
Submitting a Proposed Resolution sponsored by
JOHN P. DALEY, County Commissioner
Co-Sponsored by
ANTHONY J. PERAICA and PETER N. SILVESTRI, County Commissioners
PROPOSED RESOLUTION
PROPOSED AMENDMENT TO THE COOK COUNTY PURCHASING ACT
WHEREAS, the Purchasing Agent of Cook County is charged with the responsibility of soliciting bids
and entering into contracts for commodities and services as specified by all Cook County agencies; and
WHEREAS, the Office of the Cook County Purchasing Agent strives to serve the citizens of the County
of Cook through the use of sound, prudent, and consistent procurement practices fo r those departments
and agencies which report to the President and the Cook County Board of Commissioners; and
WHEREAS, the Office of the Cook County Purchasing Agent is committed to fulfilling the needs of
Cook County agencies in an environment in which vendors receive fair and impartial treatment in doing
business with Cook County; and
WHEREAS, the Office of the Cook County Purchasing Agent, in addition to other bureaus, departments,
and agencies of Cook County, may determine that contracts for certain commodities and services are
appropriate for procurement under tenns outlined in the issuance of a Request for Proposal, commonly
referred to as an " RFP"; and

1722

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 7, 2005

WHEREAS, the technical and detailed nature of the process for development of an effective RFP may in
certain cases require assistance, advice, or oversight from professional consultants who are compensated
accordingly for their work product; and
WHEREAS, in such cases, a conflict of interest may exist in the event that a professional consultant,
acting as either an individual or business entity and party to a contractual relationship with Cook County,
under tenns providing for services related to the preparation of an RFP, subsequentl y seeks to be awarded
additional business with Cook County in the perfonnance of duties or provision of goods and/or services
as described in the RFP; and
WHEREAS, among purchasing professionals in both the private and public sectors, commonly known
best practices in the industry are specifically designed to prevent such conflicts of interest when the
purchaser is acquiring goods and services under the aegis of an RFP process; now, therefore,
BE IT RESOLVED, by the Board of Commissioners of Cook County that the Board does hereby amend
the Cook County Purchasing Act to incorporate these industry best practices, and to prohibit the awarding
of contracts for goods and/or services to any individual or business entity under the tenns of a Request for
Proposal, when said individual or business entity was directly and substantially involved in drafting,
writing, researching or preparing the RFP and any ancillary documents related to same; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that this amendment to the Cook County Purchasing Act 1s
immediately effective upon becoming law.

Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Maldonado, moved to suspend the rules so that this
matter may be considered. The motion carried unanimously.
Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Hansen, moved that the Proposed Resolution be
referred to the Committee on Finance. (Comm. No. 271504). The motion carried unanimously.

OFFICE OF THE COUNTY CLERK
PROPOSED CONTRACT

Transmitting a Communication from
DAYID ORR, County Clerk
by
CLEM BALANOFF, Director of Elections
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to enter into a contract with Sequoia Voting Systems,
Inc., Oakland, California, for the purchase of election equipment. The contract is for 2,650 in-precinct
optical scan ballot readers, 3,000 touch-screen direct recording electronic (DRE) voting machines with a
voter verifiable paper audit trial (VVPAT) and two (2) high-speed ballot readers; as well as election
management software, support, supplemental equipment and maintenance provisions.
Reason:

The County Clerk issued a request for proposals (RFP), to which it received eleven (11)
responses. The County Clerk's office selected four (4) vendors to be finalists. The proposal
of Sequoia Voting Systems, Inc. had the lowest price of any of the best and final offers that
the County Clerk received from these vendors. Sequoia Voting Systems, Inc. has had great
success with its DRE system, which includes a voter verifiable paper audit trail (VVPAT).
They are the only company to have deployed a VVPAT in an election. Sequoia Voting
Systems, Inc. has a time-tested, widely-used optical scan system.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: None. Grant funded amount: $23,754,630.00. One time purchase. Account
established contingent upon acceptance of grant.
The Chief lnfonnation Officer has reviewed this item and concurs with this recommendation.

DEPARTMENT OF ENVIRONMENTAL CONTROL
GRANT RENEWAL APPLICATION

Transmitting a Communication, dated April 29, 2005 from
KEVIN GIVENS, Director, Department of Environmental Control
requesting authorization to apply for a grant renewal in the amount of $374,642.00 from the United States
Environmental Protection Agency (USEPA). The purpose of this grant is to provide supplemental
funding for the continued operation and maintenance of specialized air pollution monitoring sites in Cook
County pursuant to the Illinois Environmental Protection Agency Air Monitoring Plan for 2005 - 2006.
These sites measure the 2.5 micron-sized particles suspended in the air as part of a new requirement from
the USEPA and are part of a special research project to determine the quantity and composition of these
very small particles in the urban air.
This grant does not require a cash match.
The Budget Department has reviewed this item, and all requisite documents have been submitted.
Estimated Fiscal Impact: None. Grant Award: $374,642.00. Funding period : March I, 2005 through
February 28, 2006.

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Moreno, moved that the request of the Director of
the Department of Environmental Control be approved. The motion carried unanimously.

BUREAU OF FINANCE-CHIEF FINANCIAL OFFICER
CONTRACT

Transmitting a Communication, dated May 2, 2005 from
THOMAS J. GLASER, Chief Financial Officer, Bureau of Finance
On behalf of the Deferred Compensation Committee, I respectfully request approval of the Deferred
Compensation Committee's recommendation to enter into a five year contract, effective July I, 2005,
with the option to extend the contract for up to three additional periods, each period not to exceed one
year, with Nationwide Retirement Solutions (NRS), Columbus, Ohio, to provide third party administrator
services for the Cook County Deferred Compensation Plan.

1729

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 7, 2005

Standard Valuations was retained to assist the Committee in conducting a Request for Proposal (RFP) for
a full service provider. The RFP was posted on the County's and National Association of Government
Defined Contribution Administrator's (NAG DCA) websites, as well as advertisements placed in the
Chicago Tribune and Pension and Investments publications and website. There were sixteen companies
that either received the RFP from or notified Standard Valuations that they planned to respond to the
RFP. Of the sixteen firms, six firms responded to the RFP.
The Committee reviewed and rated the proposals on five categories: 1) education of employees, 2) total
annual fees charged the plan, 3) proposed local resources to support the County, 4) use of local finns, and
5) use of MBE/WBE firms. Based on these categories, the Comm ittee rated Nationwide's response the
highest and most responsive to the Committee's needs and goals.
Contract period: July I, 2005 through June 30, 20 I 0.

Commissioner Butler, seconded by Commissioner Steele, moved that the request of the Chief Financial
Officer of the Bureau of Finance be approved. The motion carried unanimously.

Emergency bridge repairs at
Lake-Cook Road at
Pfingsten Road,
Lorig Construction Corporation

$58,7 13.88
(Addition)

Repairs to the bridge deck on the Lake-Cook Bridge over the West Fork of the North Branch of the
Chicago River were needed to prevent load posting of the bridge on this high traffic volume roadway.
Advance deterioration of the bridge deck with serve corrosion of the reinforcement had resulted in a
reduction in live load carrying capacity. The condition also posed a potential safety hazard to the
motoring public, which necessitated the need for corTective action. Therefore, emergency bridge repairs
were perfonned by Lorig Construction Corporation, due to their expertise in structural repairs and
availability while a subcontractor on the Bartlett Road project.
l respectfully recommend approval by your Honorable Body.

SPEED LIMIT ZONING ORDINANCE AMENDMENT

Transmitting a Communication, dated May 6, 2005 from
WALLY S. KOS, P.E., Superintendent of Highways
Re: Speed Limit Zoning Ordinance Amendment
I respectfully submit to your Honorable Body and recommend for adoption, an ordinance amending the
Speed Limit Zoning Ordinance by delegating to the Superintendent of Highways the authority to set
reduced speed limits within construction or maintenance zones. This request is pursuant to the Illinois
Vehicle Code, as recently amended, which allows for the delegation of such authority as more fully
described in the following Ordinance Amendment.

1739

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 7, 2005

This Ordinance Amendment has been reviewed by the State' s Attorney's Office and reflects their input.
It is respectfully requested that should your Honorable Body concur in this recommendation, the
Ordinance Amendment be adopted.

05-0-32
ORDINANCE
AN ORDINANCE AMENDING THE COUNTY SPEED LIMIT ZONING ORDINANCE
This County Ordinance, Sections 11-20 and 11-22 of Chapter 11, Traffic Regulations, of the Code of
Ordinances is amended by addition of the following:
DELEGATION TO THE SUPERINTENDENT OF HIGHWAYS THE AUTHORITY TO
SET REDUCED SPEED LIMITS WITHIN CONSTRUCTION OR MAINTENANCE ZONES.
Section 11 - 19.
WHEREAS, the County of Cook, through the County Superintendent of Highways, is responsible for the
construction, reconstruction, repair and maintenance of certain public highways under the jurisdiction of
the County of Cook; and
WHEREAS, pursuant to the Illinois Vehicle Code, 625 ILCS 5/ 11-605.2, the authority to set reduced
speed limits within construction or maintenance work zones may be delegated to the Superintendent of
Highways.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT ORDAINED, that the Members of the Board of Commissioners of Cook
County hereby authorize the Superintendent of Highways to set and post reduced speed limits for
construction or maintenance zones; as defined in 625 ILCS 5/ 11-605.1; and
BE IT FURTHER ORDAINED, that such reduced speed limits shall be temporary and be in-effect and
in full force from the time appropriate signing giving notice of the reduced speed limits are erected until
such time that said signing is removed; and
BE IT FURTHER ORDAINED, that construction or maintenance zone speed limit signs shall ( 1) be of
a design approved by the Illinois Department of Transportation, (2) give proper warning that a
construction or maintenance speed zone is being approached, (3) indicate the maximum speed limit in
effect, and (4) state the amount of the minimum fine for a violation as established by 625 ILCS 5/11605.1.; and
BE IT FURTHER ORDAINED, that a record be maintained by the Highway Department naming each
location, the reduced speed limit set and posted for the construction or maintenance zone and dates during
which the reduced speed limit was in effect; and
BE IT FINALLY ORDAINED, that affected jurisdictions be notified of the changes in the posted speed
limits so that they may be properly enforced.
June 7, 2005.

Commissioner Hansen, seconded by Commissioner Moreno, moved that the Ordinance Amendment be
approved and adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

roadway from U.S. Route 45 (LaGrange Road) to 94th Avenue to include two lanes in each direction
separated by a continuous median; pavement reconstruction and widening from 94th A venue to the

median; and shall include curb and gutter, enclosed drainage system, channelization, sidewalks, lighting,
right-of-way acquisition, new at-grade railroad crossing to include crossing surface and warning devices,

AMENDED QUICK TAKE AUTHORITY RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, the Highway Department considered the desirability and importance of providing for the
improvement of West Bartlett Road under Section: 00-B 1003-05-RP and after such consideration
certified its approval of the proposed improvement to the Cook County Board of Commissioners; and
WHEREAS, the County Board on August 9, 2000 adopted a Resolution providing for the improvement
of West Bartlett Road under Section: OO-Bl003-05-RP; and
WHEREAS, having the County Board 's approval, the Cook County Superintendent of Highways caused
to be prepared proper surveys, maps, plans, specifications and estimates of cost of the proposed
improvement; and
WHEREAS, said plans and surveys require that private property be taken for such improvement pursuant
to authority granted under the Illinois Highway Code [Chapter 605 of the Tllinois Compiled Statutes
(2000), 5/5-801 ]; and
WHEREAS, the private property to be taken consists of real property legally described in the exhibits
submitted herewith; and
WHEREAS, delay caused by time consuming condemnation litigation to acquire land would result in
increased cost and inconvenience to the public; and
WHEREAS, Quick Take legal procedures will expedite the improvement and result in a scheduled
completion date.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, by the Cook County Board of Commissioners that the
Cook County Superintendent of Highways is hereby authorized, empowered and directed on behalf of the
County of Cook to seek Quick Take Authority from the State Legislature for a period of one year
pursuant to their procedures for the West Bartlett Road project.
June 7, 2005

approved and adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

CONTRACT

Transmitting a Communication from
TIMOTHY C. EVANS, Chief Judge, Circuit Court of Cook County
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to enter into a contract with Youth Outreach Services,
Chicago, Illinois, for professional services for the court's Community Circles Program, to be
administered through the Circuit Court of Cook County' s Juvenile Probation and Court Services
Department.
Reason:

The purpose of the Community Circles Program is to provide community-based drug
treatment services to delinquent minors who reside in Chicago's North Lawndale Community.
Youth Outreach Services is the lead agency for the program, supervising services provided by
designated sub-contractors, including Westside Association for Community Action, the
Chicago Youth Centers and other local substance abuse and mental health professionals. The
court anticipates serving approximately 350 minors in the next program year. The program is
an integral part of the court's award-winning continuum of services available to judges of the
Juvenile Justice Divi sion to help reduce substance abuse and delinquent behavior by minors
under the supervision of the court.
Youth Outreach Services is a not-for-profit corporation and licensed adolescent treahnent
provider and child welfare agency, accredited by the Council on Accreditation for Children
and Family Services. Youth Outreach Services has provided substance abuse treatment
services to the court under the Community Circles Program for the past three years.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: None. Grant funded amount: $304,725.00. Contract period : July 1, 2005
through June 30, 2006. (839-260 Account). Requisition No. 5839000 1.
Commissioner Daley, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri , moved that the County Purchasing Agent be
authorized to enter into the requested contract. The motion carried unanimously.
CONTRACT RENEW AL

Transmitting a Communication from
TIMOTHY C. EV ANS, Chief Judge, Circuit Court of Cook County
requesting authorization for the Purchasing Agent to renew Contract No. 02-42-1 118 with Central States
Institute of Addiction (CSI), Chicago, Illinois, an agency of Catholic Charities, for drug screening
services for the court's drug treatment court program for adults.

1758

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 7, 2005

Reason:

CSJ has provided alcohol and drug assessment, and intervention services to the court for more
than thirty (30) years, and drug screening services to the drug treatment court program since
1998. Serving the drug treatment court programs operating in the Fourth Municipal District
in Maywood and the Sixth Municipal District in Markham, CS! collects and analyzes urine
samples from drug treatment court defendants using FDA-approved procedures. Results are
reported to the court within 24 hours of collection. Rigid chain-of-custody protocols for the
samples are maintained. Re-testing of positive samples is performed to ensure accuracy at no
extra charge. The cost of each test is $30.00.

Estimated Fiscal Impact: $ 100,000.00. Contract period: August 1, 2005 through July 31 , 2006. (54 1278 Account). Requisition No. 554 10047.
Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Steele, moved that the County Purchasing Agent be
authorized to renew the requested contract. The motion carried unanimously.

Re:

Pulaski Partners, LLC
Resolution Approving Class 8 Special Exception to Abandonment

respectfully submitting this Resolution regarding Pulaski Partners, LLC's application for C lass 8 property
tax incentive for your consideration.
Pulaski Partners, LLC requests approval of the special exception to the 24 month abandonment rule under
the Class 8 Ordinance. This Resolution is required so that the company can complete its application to
the Assessor of Cook County.
Pulaski Partners, LLC' s application for a Class 8, the Resolution of the Village of Midlothian and a
Department of Planning and Development staff report have been submitted for your infonnation.
PROPOSED RESOLUTION

WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners has adopted a Real Property Assessment
Classification 8 that provides an applicant a reduction in the assessment level for a commercial facility;
and
WHEREAS, the County Board of Commissioners has received and reviewed an application from Pulaski
Partners, LLC and the Resolution from the Village of Midlothian for an abandoned commercial facility
located at 14441-45 South Cicero Avenue, Midlothian, Cook County, Illinois, Property Index Number 2810- 108-035-0000; and
WHEREAS, Class 8 requires the validation by the County Board of the shortened period of qualifying
abandonment in cases where the commercial facility has been abandoned for less than 24 consecutive
months upon purchase ; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners has detem1ined that the building was abandoned
for 12 months at the time of application, and that special circumstances are present.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, by the Pres ident and Board of Commissioners of the
County of Cook, State of Illinois, that the President and Board of Commissioners indicate their approval
for the filing of an application for a Cook County Real Estate Classification 8 abatement incentive to the
company for an abandoned commercial facility located at 14441-45 South Cicero A venue, Midlothian,
Cook County, Illinois, under the provision for abandonment of less than 24 months; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the County Clerk is hereby authori zed and directed to forward a
certified copy of this Resolution to the Office of the Cook County Assessor.

PROPOSED RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners has adopted a Real Property Assessment
Classification 6b that provides an applicant a reduction in the assessment level for an industrial facility;
and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners has received and reviewed an application from
Elizabeth 120, LLC for a facility located in unincorporated Elk Grove Township at 120 Elizabeth Drive,
Arlington Heights, Illinois, Property Index Number 08-26-202-006-0000; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners has determined that the Class 6b is necessary for
development to occur on the subject property and beneficial to the local company; and
WHEREAS, the Cook County Board of Commissioners has determined that the building was abandoned
for 8 months at the time of purchase and that special circumstances; including the property not being well
maintained and in a state of disrepair and in need of substantial renovation are present.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, by the President and Board of Commissioners of the
County of Cook, State of Illinois, that the President and Board of Commissioners find that Elizabeth 120,
LLC's industrial use of the property is necessary and beneficial to the local economy and that they
support and consent to the application for a Class 6b for abandoned industrial facility located at 120
Elizabeth Drive, Arlington Heights, Unincorporated Elk Grove Township, under the provision for
abandonment of less than 24 months; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the County Clerk is hereby authorized and directed to forward a

Department of Public Health.
Every five years, all state recognized local public health departments are required to perfom1 an
organizational assessment and to develop a community health plan based on a community health
assessment. This process is necessary for Cยทe rtification status and funding through the Illinois Department
of Public Health 's Local Health Protecti on G rant.
The date for the Department of Public Health to submit this information to the Illi nois Department of
Public Health is June 24, 2005.
Prior to submission, the local governing board is asked to acknowledge and adopt the written document.
Currently, the amount the Department of Public Health receives from the annual Local Health Protecti on
Grant is $ 1,899,632.00. Also, certification status provides the department with preferential consideration
for funding from many other Illino is Department of Public Health grant program s.

GRANT A WARD RENEWAL
Transmitting a Communication, dated May 2, 2005 from
MICHAEL F. SHEAHAN, Sheriff of Cook County
by
THOMAS K. DONAHUE, Executive Director, Chicago HIDTA
requesting authorization to renew a grant in the amount of $5,404,726.00 from the Office of National
Drug Control Policy (ONDCP). The purpose of this grant is the continued funding of the Chicago High
Intensity Drug Trafficking Area (HIDTA) program. The mission of the Chicago HIDTA is to combat
drug trafficking and gang activity in the designated areas of Cook County.

This award is the annual renewal of the HIDTA program. The budget process begins with the Office of
National Drug Control Policy awarding funds to the existing HIDTA 's nationwide. This grant is 100%
federally funded with no matching County funds.

Commissioners in the amount of $5,404,726.00. Authorization for a supplemental grant was given on
February I , 2005 in the amount of $ 1,321,952.00.

OFFICE OF THE COUNTY TREASURER
CREDIT CARD PAYMENT SERVICES
Transmitting a Communication, dated May I 0, 2005 from
MARIA PAPPAS, Cook County Treasurer
Pursuant to 50 lLCS 345/1 et seq., the Treasurer's Office is seeking approval to offer credit card payment
services to the taxpayers of Cook County. The Treasurer's Office respectfully requests that the County
Board hold the requisite public hearings to detennine whether the acceptance of credit card payments to
satisfy real property tax obligations is in the best interests of the citizens and governmental administration
of Cook County.

1780

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 7, 2005

A third-party service provider can offer this service to the taxpayers of Cook County at no cost to the
County. Cardholders who choose to pay by credit card would incur a convenience fee for the service.
The convenience fee would wholly offset the costs of processing the transaction and be paid directly to
the service provider. For purposes of real estate tax collections the payment of multiple tax bills in a
single transaction is prohibited.

Commissioner Butler, seconded by Commissioner Steele, moved that the communication be referred to
the Committee on Finance. (Comm. No. 271496). The motion carried unanimously.

SECTION 13
Your Committee was presented with the Fiscal Year 2005 Appropriation Trial Balance for the period
ending March 31, 2005, of the County of Cook, as submitted by the Bureau of Finance.
Walter Knorr, County Comptroller, provided an explanation of the report's key findings. Mr. Knorr stated
that spending in each major fund was at or below projections after conclusion of one-third of Fiscal Year
2005. The percentage of expenditures for each fund as of March 31, 2005, were as follows: Corporate 24.8%, Public Safety - 26.0%, and Health - 30.2%.

COMMISSIONER HANSEN, SECONDED BY COMMISSIONER SILVESTRI, MOVED TO
RECEIVE AND FILE THE APPROPRIATION TRIAL BALANCE FOR THE PERIOD ENDING
MARCH 31, 2005. THE MOTION CARRIED.

SIMS, THE MOTION CARRIED AND THE MEETING WAS ADJOURNED.

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 7, 2005

271172

THE BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS CONVENE A DISCOVERY HEARING TO
FORMALLY RECE IVE A STATUS REPORT ON THE U.S. JUSTICE DEPARTMENT
REQUEST TO EXHUME THE BODY OF EMMETT TILL (PROPOSED RESOLUTION).
Submitting a Proposed Resolution Sponsored by Bobbie L. Steele, County Commissioner;
Co-sponsored by Deborah Sims, County Commissioner
PROPOSED RESOLUTION
WHEREAS, on August 28, 1955, 14 year old Chicagoan Emmett Till was kidnapped from
his uncle's home in Money, Mississippi ; and
WHEREAS, on August 31, 1955 his murdered body was discovered; and
WHEREAS, the kidnapping and murder of Emmett Till captured international attention and
his Mother Mamie Till-Mobley led a personal campaign for justice; and
WHEREAS, two men, store owner Roy Bryant and his half brother, J W. Milam were
charged and acquitted of the murder. They later boasted about the crime several months later
according to Eye's On the Prize authored by Juan Williams; and
WHEREAS, on Tuesday, May 3, 2005 it was revealed that the U.S. Department of Justice
and the FBI requested Cook County Judge Paul Biebel, Jr. approve an order to remove Till' s
body from the Burr Oaks Cemetery in Alsip, Illinois; and
WHEREAS, the State of Mississippi has never conducted an autopsy on Emmett Till, and
during the trial, a Sheriff in the State of Mississippi stated the body was not Till's according
to Eyes on the Prize authored by Juan Williams; and
WHEREAS, Cook County Judge Paul Biebel , Jr. signed a court order requiring the removal
of Emmet Till 's body from its grave; and
WHEREAS, there is a reported split among family members and the general public on how
best to proceed; and
WHEREAS, no intergovernmental statement have been prepared within the State of Illinois
and Cook County to direct the courts on how best to proceed and to consider its jurisdictional
matter.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that no action be taken on the exhumation of
Emmett Till until the County of Cook thoroughly reviews the request from the U.S.
Department of Justice; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners, through
its respective committees, convene a Discovery Hearing to formally receive a status report on
the U.S Justice Department's request to exhume the body of Emmett Till and to invite the
Cook County Chief Medical Examiner Edmund Donoghue and his forensic team to share
with the Cook County Board of Commissioners his office's expectations, their process for
evidence gathering and the racial and professional makeup of his team .
*Referred to the Department of Corrections Subcommittee on 05/ 17/OS.

1858

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 7, 2005

Chainnan Steele delivered the following statement: There has been a new development in the Emmett
Till case and action has already been taken. However, the Board will appreciate any updated infonnation
that can be provided. The United States Department of Justice, the Federal Bureau of Investigation (FBI)
and the State of Mississippi are involved in the investigation of this case. Emmett Till 's mother labored
and protested over forty years to get this case re-opened. Recently, Congressman Bobby Rush intervened
and requested that the United States Department of Justice pursue this investigation. Congressman Rush
was unable to be here today, but he wanted the Board to move forward to inform the public of the
ongoing investigation. The intent of this hearing is to respond to some of the questions that have been
brought to Chairman Steele's attention regarding both the exhumation process which commenced today,
and the other procedures which will take place subsequently.
Vice Chairman Hansen inquired whether the Board has any jurisdiction to direct the courts or to review
requests from the United States Department of Justice. He further stated that it was his understanding that
the Board has no jurisdiction over any court order.
Patrick T. Driscoll, Jr., Deputy State's Attorney, Chief of the Civil Actions Bureau of the State's
Attorney's Office, responded that the County of the crime's occurrence has jurisdiction over this case.
Mr. Driscoll further stated the following: The FBI is involved in this case. Exhumation was perfonned
pursuant to court order. As a legislative body, the Committee may request infonnation from any source,
however, it is questionable whether the recipient of that request is required to answer. The FBI is paying
the cost of exhumation; the cost of both interment and delivery of the body is being paid by the Federal
Government.
Chainnan Steele asked the Secretary to the Board to call upon the registered public speakers:
I.
2.
3.

Ev Angel (Mamadee) - YHWIH new BN
George Blakemore - Concerned Citizen
John Paul Jones - Greater Englewood Community & Family Task Force

Communication No. 271172. The motion carried.

Corrections Subcommittee request that the State's Attorney's Office report periodically to the
Subcommittee regarding the proceedings of the Emmett Till case, and that this information be
supplied to all Members of the Cook County Board of Commissioners. The motion carried.
Commissioner Suffredin moved to adjourn the meeting, seconded by Commissioner Maldonado.

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 7, 2005

REPORT OF THE STROGER AND CERMAK HOSPITALS SUBCOMMITTEE
May 26, 2005
The Honorable,
The Board of Commissioners of Cook County

ATTENDANCE
Present:

Chairman Maldonado, Vice Chairman Silvestri, Commissioners Butler, Murphy, Peraica and
Steele (6)

Absent:

Commissioner Moreno ( 1)

Also
Present:

Commissioners Claypool, Daley and Quigley (3); Daniel H. Winship, M.D. - Chief, Bureau
of Health Services; Martin Grant - Director of Pharmacy, Oak Forest Hospital of Cook
County; Johnny Brown - Chief Operating Officer, Stroger Hospital of Cook County; Dan
Martin - Deputy Chief, Bureau of Health Services; Bernard Scavella - Deputy Director of
Support Services, Stroger Hospital of Cook County; and Mark Kilgallon - Chief, Bureau of
Human Resources

Ladies and Gentlemen:
Your Stroger and Cermak Hospitals Subcommittee of the Board of Commissioners of Cook County met
pursuant to notice on Thursday, May 26, 2005 at the hour of I :30 P.M. in the Board Room, Room 569,
County Building, 118 North Clark Street, Chicago, Illinois.
Your Subcommittee has considered the following item:
1.

To hear a presentation by the Bureau of Health Services on the severely long waiting time many
patients of the community health care clinics experience to receive their prescription medications.

Chainnan Maldonado stated that the purpose of this meeting is to hear a presentation by the Bureau of
Health Services on the severely long waiting periods that many patients experience to receive their
prescription medications. Chairman Maldonado further stated this meeting is for informational purposes
only.
Commissioner Murphy noted that Oak Forest Hospital of Cook County is doing a remarkable job filling
prescriptions. She asked whether it would be possible to fax prescriptions from Stroger Hospital of Cook
County to be filled at Oak Forest Hospital of Cook County.
Chairman Maldonado replied that the mail order prescription drugs program was reinstated in March and
the Bureau of Health Services is filling fifteen thousand prescriptions each day.
Daniel H. Winship, M.D., Chief of the Bureau of Health Services, commented that during 2004 the
Bureau of Health Services filled 2.9 million prescriptions and at its current pace will fill over 3.8 million
prescriptions in 2005. The prescriptions could be filled in a more timely manner if ample space and
personnel were available. The Bureau of Health Services fills ten thousand prescriptions per day and the
largest request come from Stroger Hospital of Cook County and the Fantus Clinic. The national bench
mark for productivity in filling prescriptions is about 250 per eight hour shift with a phannacist and two
phannacist technicians. The Bureau of Health Services averages about 400 per eight hour shift per
pharmacist and two pharmacist technicians.

1860

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 7, 2005

Dr. Winship noted that the Bureau of Health Services has included twelve new positions in the 2005
budget and there are vacancies throughout the phannacy department. The Bureau of Health Services is in
the process of recruiting pharmacists and phannacist technicians. The Bureau of Health Services,
Department of Personnel has taken several steps to improve the financial support of the phannacy
department, the wages for phannacists and pharmacist technicians have again fallen behind at the Bureau
of Health Services. The Bureau of Health Services has advertised for pharmacists, however, the starting
salary for graduating phannacists who apply at Walgreen's, CVS or other hospitals salaries would be
higher than the Bureau of Health Services would pay. The Bureau of Health Service' s starting salary is
not competitive for recruiting ofphannacists or phannacist technicians.
Vice Chairman Silvestri asked how many such vacancies are in the Bureau of Health Services.
Dr. Winship replied there are twenty-four vacant pharmacist positions. There are sixteen staff pharmacists
and eight supervisor management positions for a total of twenty-four positions.
Johnny Brown, Chief Operating Officer, Stroger Hospital of Cook County, stated that the patients have an
option to fill their prescription at either any local drug store or at the Bureau of Health Services facilities.
The Medicaid patients will pay out of pocket expense for prescriptions filled off-site.
Dan Martin, Deputy Chief, Bureau of Health Services, stated that the Bureau of Health Services
purchases drugs for the outpatients from the 340B program. There are strict regulations regarding the
purchase of drugs. The restrictions are that drugs can only be purchased and used at the sites that are
designated as disproportionately shared hospitals and federally qualified health care clinics such as: Ryan
White Grantees, Federal Health Care Centers, and look-a-like facilities that are pre-approved by the
Federal Government. The regulations that currently exist are governed by the National Association of
Public Hospitals and Pharmacies Coalition.
Mr. Martin continued to reiterate that all out-patient phannacy purchases are purchased through the 340B
program. However, Medicaid patients can purchase phannaceuticals at any pharmacy that accepts
Medicaid. The Bureau of Health Services was able to negotiate with the State of Illinois to receive
enhanced reimbursement under the Intergovernmental Transfer Agreement for phannacy services and has
started billing for phannacy services. The Bureau of Health Services would like to keep the Public Aid
and Medicaid/Medicare patients in the system to assist with offsetting the cost.
Chainnan Maldonado asked about the amount of overtime for the phannacy department last year.
Mr. Brown stated about ten million dollars ($10,000,000) was spent for overtime last year.
Chainnan Maldonado asked how the Bureau of Health Services solicits the patients to use the mail order
prescription fonns.
Mr. Martin stated that the patients fill their prescriptions at the Bureau of Health Services and mail order
prescription pamphlets are inserted in their bags. The Bureau of Health Services has sixteen employees
traveling throughout the County's thirty-one clinics. The representatives meet with the administration to
coordinate a convenient time frame in which to infonn patients about the mail order prescription program.
Commissioner Murphy inquired about the number of employees at the phamrncies.
Bernard Scavella, Deputy Director of Support Services, replied that the Bureau of Health Services
employs four out-patient phannacists, and is staffed by two pharmacy managers and one supervisor.

186 1

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 7, 2005

Commissioner Daley asked the Bureau of Health Services how many pharmacists are needed to solve the
problem of the long wait for prescription drugs.
Mr. Scavella stated that if the Bureau of Health Services were to hire more pharmacists, there would not
be adequate space to accommodate the additional staff.
Commissioner Daley asked the Bureau of Health Services whether there is a tracking system in place to
log the waiting period to fill patient's prescriptions.
Mr. Scavella stated that the Bureau of Health Services has a tracking system at Stroger Hospital of Cook
County and the Fantus Clinic. The system has various categories of prescriptions that are filled.
Approximately sixty-eight percent (68%) of the prescriptions are new, twenty-six percent (26%) of the
prescriptions are refills and four and one half percent (4.5%) of the prescriptions are from discharged
patients. The Bureau of Health Services prioritizes the emergency room prescriptions and guarantees an
eight hour turn around time. Discharged patient's prescriptions are guaranteed a two to three hour turn
around time. The emergency prescriptions from the other Bureau of Health Services clinics have a turn
around time of eight hours.
Commissioner Steele asked whether in the hiring of pharmacy personnel, they could begin at a higher
level rate of pay, as was done at the Veterans Administration.
ยท
Mr. Martin stated that the current salary structure only allows the Bureau of Health Services to go up to
Step 5 positions within the phannacy category and does not allow the Bureau of Health Services to go
beyond that step.
Mark Kilgallon, Director, Bureau of Human Resources stated that an increase of ten million dollars
($10,000,000) was given to the pharmacy staff to bring the Bureau of Health Service' s salaries in line
with other institutions. The County is not competitive with the current market; however, the Bureau of
Health Services is presently negotiating with the phannacy unions. In regards to hiring staff at the
advance step levels, the increase in salary has to be included in the budget and all open salaries are
budgeted at the Step 1 level.
Commissioner Peraica asked what could be done to reduce patients ' waiting periods for prescription
drugs.
Dr. Winship noted that the Bureau of Health Services is implementing a provider order entry program in
the Cemer System. This program will have speed, safety and correctness in the interpretation of the
written prescriptions from the staff and the speed to get it to the phannacy department.
Chainnan Maldonado reiterated the question of whether the waiting periods for prescription drugs would
decrease due to the installing of the Cerner System.
Mr. Martin noted that the patient would have the option of traveling to any pharmacy at the Bureau of
Health Services and the patient would get an electronic print-out of his or her prescription. The
pharmacist and phannacist technician will be able to understand the electronic print-out prescription
forms from the physicians.
Dr. Winship stated that the program has been installed at Oak Forest Hospital of Cook County and is
perfonning beautifully. The program will arrive at Stroger Hospital of Cook County in the summer and
will be installed throughout the Bureau.

1862

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 7, 2005

Chairman Maldonado asked about the recruiting of Latino phannacists and pharmacist technicians.
Dr. Winship replied that there are Latino pharmacists at the Bureau of Health Services. We will be
delighted to recruit bi-lingual phannacists and pharmacist technicians.
Chainnan Maldonado stated that he has never seen advertisement for bi-lingual and Latino pharmacists or
pharmacist technicians.
Dr. Winship stated that the Bureau of Health Services advertises in the newspapers.

05-R-243
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOHN H. STROGER, JR.
PRESIDENT OF THE COOK COUNTY BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, in Federal Fiscal Year 2004, the Community Development Block Grant Program (CDBG)
provided funds for thousands of activities, assisting over 23 million persons and households through such
activities as expanding homeownership activities, eliminating slums and blighting influences, improving
infrastructure such as roads, water and sewer systems, libraries, community centers, homeless housing
facilities, employment training, transportation services, crime awareness, and business and job creation;
and
WHEREAS, Cook County uses CDBG funds in the amount of $12,622,585 for Program Year 2005 for
the above cited community and economic development revitalization programs; and

1863

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 7, 2005

WHEREAS, the President's FY 2006 budget proposes to completely eliminate the CDBG Program; and
WHEREAS, should such a proposal be enacted, it would have a devastating effect on Cook County; and
WHEREAS, the undersigned urge the President and the Congress of the United States to continue to
support and to fully fund the Community Development Block Grant (CDBG) Program.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County hereby calls on Congress to preserve
the Community Development Block Grant (CDBG) Program and provide FY 2006 funding at program
year 2004 levels or at least $4.7 billion overall, with no less than $4.5 billion in formula funding; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be sent to the leadership of both
Houses and the entire Illinois Congressional Delegation.

Approved and adopted this 7th day of June 2005.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAVID ORR, County Clerk

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Murphy, moved that the Resolution be approved
and adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

05-R-244
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOHN H. STROGER, JR.
PRESIDENT OF THE COOK COUNTY BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, we, as a nation concerned with an uncertain economy, must make a concerted effort to
recognize the value of continued input of local governments in dealing with the local needs of Workforce
Development and helping employers find capable candidates to fill vacancies; and
WHEREAS, as public officials, we must make certain that we channel every available Workforce dollar
into our local communities in order to support the optimum number of Dislocated, Adult, and Youth
clients seeking assistance in training and transition, until retention of gainful employment is achieved; and
WHEREAS, we must make certain that we channel every available workforce dollar into our local
communities in order to support the optimum number of employers who are seeking to recruit, train and
retain their productive and contributing employees, who reside in our communities; and
WHEREAS, the U.S . Senate Committee on Health, Education, Labor and Pensions (H.E.L.P.), has
passed a senate bill for Workforce Investment Act (WIA) Re-Authorization Legislation on May 18,
2005 which restores much of the local control, business led Workforce Boards, and the funding streams
and formula allocation; and

1864

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 7, 2005

WHEREAS, the Cook County President's Office of Employment and Training (POET) and its staff,
have administered this federal program on our behalf, successfully serving tens of thousands of people
over the last three decades and previous incarnations, helping the unemployed and those needing
additional skills to obtain new jobs or move upward in their occupation.

NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that we, the President and the Cook County Board of
Commissioners gathered here, this 7th day of June, 2005, do hereby proclaim our support of this bill as
passed on May 18, 2005 by the Senate H.E.L.P. Committee which includes language to preserve the
existing funding streams and local authority. We strenuously support efforts to return this program to the
fundamental concepts under which it was originally authorized; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that when this measure goes to conference, we proclaim our support to
pass this measure in principle and structure, and if possible, restore funding to current levels; and

BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that we encourage our colleagues in other de liberate bodies to take
efforts and legislative action in joining the Cook County Board of Commissioners in support of restoring
full WIA funding levels, retaining local control and input, and retaining the fonnula allocation segments
as in existing legislation; and

BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be sent to the leadership of both
Houses and the entire Illinois Congressional Delegation.
Approved and adopted this 7th day of June 2005.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR. , President
Cook County Board of Commissioners

05-R-246
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOHN H. STROGER, JR., PRESIDENT, EARLEAN COLLINS,

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 7, 2005

WHEREAS, on the morning of May 16, 2005, Almighty God in His infinite wisdom called home his
servant, Senator Margaret Smith at the age of eighty-two; and
WHEREAS, Senator Margaret Smith was born in Chicago, Illinois in 1922 where she lived and engaged
in a lifetime of impeccable public service; and
WHEREAS, Senator Margaret Smith confessed Christ at an early age and was a member of the
Bethesaida Baptist Church; and
WHEREAS, Senator Margaret Smith graduated from DuSable High School and Tennessee State
University in Nashville and has an honorary Doctor of Humanities degree from the Chicago Baptist
Institute and was recognized throughout the United States and nationally for her humanitarian work; and
WHEREAS, Senator Margaret Smith married her late husband Fred Smith in 1955 who served 36 years
in the Illinois General Assembly; and
WHEREAS, Senator Margaret Smith was elected to the Illinois House of Representatives in 1980 to
1983 and the Illinois Senate in 1984 to 2002 where she served a total of 22 years; and
WHEREAS, Senator Margaret Smith was highly admired and affectionately known among her
colleagues as 'ยทLady Margaret"; and
WHEREAS, throughout her legislative career she championed the fight to improve services for women
and children. Her primary focus was on public health and welfare and some of her proposals served as
models for national welfare refonn; and
WHEREAS, Senator Margaret Smith was a leader in promoting African American history in Illinois as
well as throughout the country; and
WHEREAS, Senator Margaret Smith authorized legislation commissioning the sculpture of statues of
Adelbert H. Roberts and Dr. Martin Luther King, Jr. She participated in and promoted Black History
Month and the Martin Luther King, Jr. holiday throughout the country; and
WHEREAS, Senator Margaret Smith leaves to cherish her memory all who knew and loved her and a
legacy for future generations of compassion and commitment to public service.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Board of Commissioners of Cook County, hereby
expresses its sincere sorrow and extends deepest sympathy to the family and friends of Senator Margaret
Smith; and

1867

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 7, 2005

BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that this text be spread upon the official proceedings of the Cook
County Board of Commissioners, and that a suitable copy shall be provided to the family of Senator
Margaret Smith in recognition of her selfless service to advance the cause of humanity which inspired the
lives of the people of the State of Illinois, Chicago, Cook County, and even this nation.
Approved and adopted this 7th day of June 2005.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners

Transmitting a Communication, dated May 25, 2005 from
WALTER K. KNORR, County Comptroller
Transmitted herewith for your consideration is a Resolution providing for the transfer of $1 , 110,092.00
from the County's Motor Fuel Tax Fund to the County's Circuit Court Automation Fund for the Fiscal
Year 2005.
Your approval of this Resolution is recommended.

OS-R-247
RESOLUTION
A RESOLUTION providing for the transfer of funds from the Motor Fuel Tax Fund of
the County of Cook, Illinois to the Circuit Court Automation Fund of the County of
Cook, Illinois
PREAMBLES
WHEREAS, Section 6(a) of Article VII of the 1970 Constitution of the State of Illinois provides that a
"County which has a Chief Executive Officer elected by the electors of the County .. .(is) a Home Rule
Unit" and The County of Cook, Illinois (the "County") has a Chief Executive Officer elected by the
electors of the County and is therefore a Home Rule Unit and may, under the powers granted by said
Section 6(a) of Article VII of said Constitution of 1970, exercise any power and perform any function
pertaining to its government and affairs; and
WHEREAS, the County has previously established a Motor Fuel Tax Fund of the County (the "Motor
Fuel Tax Fund"); and
WHEREAS, Article 5, Division 1, Section 5-70 I.I 0 of the Illinois Highway Code, as amended (Ill. Rev.
Stat. (1991 ), Ch. 121,~ 5-701- l 0), authorizes the County to use any motor fuel tax money allotted to the
County for the purpose of paying any and all expenditures resulting from activities conducted by the
Circuit Court located in the County and for the further purpose of paying any and all expenditures
resulting from the activities of any County department which has a relation to highways located within the
County; and

1868

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 7, 2005

WHEREAS, moneys existing in the Motor Fuel Tax Fund may be used to pay any and all expenditures
resulting from the activities conducted by the Circuit Court located in the County and for the further
purpose of paying any and all expenditures resulting from the activities of any County department which
has a relation to highways located within the County by transferring such moneys, in whole or in part, to
the Circuit Court Automation Fund of the County (the "Automation Fund"); and
WHEREAS, moneys will be available in the Motor Fuel Tax Fund for transfer to the Automation Fund
during the Fiscal Year 2005; and
WHEREAS, the County has detem1ined it to be in its best interest to transfer $1, 110,092.00 from the
Motor Fuel Tax Fund to the Automation Fund.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT AND IT IS HEREBY RESOLVED, by the Board of Commissioners of
the County of Cook, Illinois, as follows:
Section 1. Incorporation of Preambles. The Board hereby finds that all of the recitals
contained in the preambles to this Resolution are full, true, and correct and does hereby incorporate them
into this Resolution by this reference.
Section 2. Authorization. It is hereby found and detennined that the Board has been authorized
by law to transfer a sum of $ 1, 110,092.00 from the Motor Fuel Tax Fund to the Automation Fund.
Section 3. Transfer of Funds. The Treasurer of the County is hereby directed to transfer from
the Motor Fuel Tax Fund a sum of $ 1, 110,092.00 which amount is to be placed to the credit of the
Automation Fund for expenditures resulting from activities conducted by the Circuit Court of the County
and for highway related County department expenditures for the Fiscal Year 2005 .
Section 4. Filing of the Resolution. The Board hereby directs the C lerk of the County to file a
certified copy of this Resolution with the Treasurer of the County and the Treasurer is hereby directed to
cause the transfer of moneys as provided by, and for the purpose set forth, in this Resolution.
Section 5. Severability. If any section, paragraph or provision of this Resolution shall be held to
be invalid or unenforceable for any reason, the invalidity or unenforceability of such section, paragraph or
provision shall not affect any of the remaining provisions of this Resolution.
Section 6. Repealer. All ordinances, resolutions or orders, or parts thereof, in conflict with the
provisions of this Resolution are to the extent of such conflict hereby repealed.
Section 7. Constitutional Power of the County. This Resolution is adopted pursuant to the
constitutional powers of the County as a home rule unit notwithstanding any provisions of the Illinois
Revised Statutes to the contrary.
Section 8. Effective Date. The Board hereby finds that this Resolution shall be in full force and
effect immediately upon its passage by the Board and approval by the President of the Board.
PRESENTED, PASSED, APPROVED AND RECORDED, by the County of Cook, lllinois, a
home rule unit of government, this 7th day of June 2005.

1869

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 7, 2005

Approved and adopted this 7th day of June 2005.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAYID ORR, County Clerk

Commissioner Silvestri, seconded by Commissioner Butler, moved that the Resolution be approved and
adopted. The motion carried.
Commissioner Peraica voted "present" on the above item.

RESOLUTION

05-R-252
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by

THE HONORABLE JOHN H. ST ROGER, JR.
PRESIDENT OF THE COOK COUNTY BOARD OF COMMISSIONERS
Co-Sponsored by

THE HONORABLE JERRY BUTLER, FORREST CLAYPOOL, EARLEAN COLLINS,
JOHN P. DALEY, ELIZABETH ANN DOODY GORMAN, GREGG GOSLIN,
CARL R. HANSEN, ROBERTO MALDONADO, JOSEPH MARIO MORENO,
JOAN PATRICIA MURPHY, ANTHONY J. PERAICA, MIKE QUIGLEY,
PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS, BOBBIE L. STEELE
AND LARRY SUFFREDIN, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, Almighty God in His infinite wisdom has called prolific, genre-spanning lyricist and
composer, Oscar Brown, Jr. from our midst; and

1874

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 7, 2005

WHEREAS, a native of Chicago, Oscar Brown, Jr. grew up in the Bronzeville community and found his
calling early in life; at the young age of fifteen, he made his professional debut as part of the national
radio program, "Secret City"; and
WHEREAS, Oscar Brown's father, a real estate attorney and agent, impressed upon Oscar the
importance of reaching back to help others in need and of being cognizant of the real meaning of the word
"community" and the need to work together for the benefit of the collective body; and
WHEREAS, Oscar Brown, Jr. viewed music and songwriting as a way to bring people together, enrich
their lives and lift their spirits, especially during the turbulent 1960s and 70s; and
WHEREAS, Oscar Brown, Jr. never subscribed to the theory that "some people just cannot be helped,
rather, he believed that " ... every human has some potential in them". To Oscar Brown, Jr., the
expression " hip" became an acronym for " Human Improvement Potential" because he always encouraged
people to tap into their "over-looked" gifts; and
WHEREAS, whether as a civil rights activist or in the music arena, Oscar Brown, Jr. provoked deep
thought and introspection; and
WHEREAS, with the passing of Oscar Brown, Jr., we have lost a brilliant, prolific and socially conscious
voice whose thought provoking lyrics and performances brought smiles of joy to countless admirers
around the globe. Mr. Brown was a man who improved his community by freely sharing his aweinspiring gifts with others.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners, on behalf
of the more than five million residents of Cook County, does hereby express its deepest condolences and
most heartfelt sympathy to the family as well as the many friends and loved ones of legendary jazz
perfonner, Oscar Brown, Jr.
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be tendered to the family of
Oscar Brown, Jr., so that his historic legacy may be so honored and ever cherished.
Approved and adopted this 7th day of June 2005.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DA YID ORR, County Clerk

adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE ELIZABETH ANN DOODY GORMAN, COUNTY COMMISSIONER

THE HONORABLE JOHN H. STROGER, JR., PRESIDENT, JERRY BUTLER,
FORREST CLAYPOOL, EARLEAN COLLINS, JOHN P. DALEY,

AND LARRY SUFFREDIN, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, Almighty God in His infinite wisdom has taken from our midst Ann Quinlan, born into life
on January 12, 1940, born into eternity on April 29, 2005 ; and
WHEREAS, Ann was the beloved wife of Ed Quinlan and cherished mother of Patty (Shu), Michael and
Kim (Stepanek); and
WHEREAS, Ann and her husband Ed moved to the Mount Greenwood neighborhood in 1958 eager to
start a new life as a new bride and mother; and
WHEREAS, Ann was a respected and active member of the Queen of Martyrs Parish and became very
active in all of the activities of the church and school; and
WHEREAS, Ann's sense of family, friendship, and community are a testament to the deep caring and
love she felt for others as evidenced in organizing and starring in a Cafe Royale production which was the
school 's major fundraiser, running the annual carnival to help pay the expenses of the school and church,
and building the church garden to memorialize children who become angels; and
WHEREAS, Ann' s community involvement didn' t stop there when she organized and launched the
" Friend in Deed" program to reach out to those who need help, and volunteered countless hours at local
shelters to feed the hungry; and
WHEREAS, Ann will greatly be missed and her family, friends, and community will truly feel the loss
of her presence amongst them.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the President and Cook County Board of
Commissioners join her family and friends in mourning the death of Ann Quinlan and express their
deepest and most heartfelt condolences to her family; and

1877

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 7, 2005

BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the text of this Resolution be spread across the official
proceedings of this Honorable Body and that a suitable copy of same be tendered to the family of Ann
Quinlan.
Approved and adopted this 7th day of June 2005.

05-R-255
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE ELIZABETH ANN DOODY GORMAN, COUNTY COMMISSIONER
Co-Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOHN H. STROGER, JR., PRESIDENT, JERRY BUTLER,
FORREST CLAYPOOL, EARLEAN COLLINS, JOHN P. DALEY,
GREGG GOSLIN, CARL R. HANSEN, ROBERTO MALDONADO,
JOSEPH MARIO MORENO, JOAN PATRICIA MURPHY, ANTHONY J. PERAICA,
MIKE QUIGLEY, PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS, BOBBIE L. STEELE
AND LARRY SUFFREDIN, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, the Members of the Cook County Board of Commissioners are proud to recognize those
individuals who make significant contributions to society through reporting news; and
WHEREAS, Charles Richards is retiring after 35 years as publisher of the Regional Press; and
WHEREAS, Charles began working for the Regional Press while he was in high school, working his
way up through the ranks as a reporter, photographer, editor, ad manager, circulation manager and finally
purchased the paper from his father, Carl in 1970; and
WHEREAS, for the first six years of his tenure as publisher, Charles worked 80 hours per week handling
the responsibilities of editor, darkroom operation and production manager in his effort to deliver quality
and accurate reporting of news covering the City of Palos Heights; and
WHEREAS, by 1980, Charles had increased the total sales of the paper tenfold making it the most
successful and read local newspaper in the southwest suburban area adding Orland Park to the news
coverage area; and
WHEREAS, six years later, Charles purchased a neighborhood weekly named the Reporter serving
municipalities adjacent to those served by the Regional Press; and

1878

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 7, 2005
WHEREAS, during his career, Charles was elected to two terms as President of the Palos Chamber of
Commerce, member of the board of directors of the Calumet Ben Franklin Club and President of the
Cook County Suburban Publishers Association, later taking over as Treasurer of that group; and
WHEREAS, the most significant and gratifying accomplishment of Charles Ri chards' career was being
named the Illinoi s Press Association's Best Small Weekly Newspaper in Illinois five times.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the President and Cook County Board of
Commissioners congratulates Charles Richards on a distinguished career and sends their best wishes for
an enjoyable retirement.
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that the text of this Resolution be spread across the official proceeding
of this Honorable Body and that a suitable copy of same be presented to the family of Charles Richards.

Approved and adopted this 7th day of June 2005.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAYID ORR, County Clerk

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved that the Resolution be approved
and adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

05-R-260
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JERRY BUTLER, COUNTY COMMISSIONER
Co-Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOHN H. STROGER, JR., PRESIDENT, FORREST CLAYPOOL,
EARLEAN COLLINS, JOHN P. DALEY, ELIZABETH ANN DOODY GORMAN,
GREGG GOSLIN, CARL R. HANSEN, ROBERTO MALDONADO,
JOSEPH MARIO MORENO, JOAN PATRICIA MURPHY, ANTHONY J. PERAICA,
MIKE Q UIGLEY, PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS, BOBBIE L. STEELE
AND LARRY SUFFREDIN, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
WHEREAS, Hazel Renfroe was born in Chicago, Illinois on Sunday, June 18, 1905, she graduated from
Bowen High School, received her Bachelor's Degree from the University of Chicago and a Masters of
Science Degree in Art Education from the Illinoi s lnstitute of Technology; and

WHEREAS, Hazel Renfroe studied Art History and Critical Analysis at the Sorbonne in Paris, France for
a year on scholarship, studied painting at the Academic Julian and pursued interior design at
Northwestern University; and
WHEREAS, Ms. Renfroe's lifelong passion was teaching, receiving her teacher' s certificate from
C hicago Non na] College. Hazel Renfroe rose through the ranks from Elementary Art Instructor to
Supervisor of Arts while teaching at various Chi cago schools throughout her career; and
WHEREAS, Hazel Renfroe was initiated in the Lambda Chapter of Delta Sigma Theta in 1927 and was
three times elected their President; and

WHEREAS, Hazel Renfroe won her Women 's Defense Corps of America Uniform, during World War II
by volunteering I 00 hours to the Red Cross, she taught gas mask and messenger courses, and acted as
chaperone for military parties in southern Illinois camps. Ms. Renfroe sold War Savings Stamps and
Bonds for which the Treasury Department gave her special recognition for exceeding the million-dollar
mark in sales; and

WHEREAS, Hazel Renfroe is a founding member of the South Side Community Art Center,
Metropolitan Council of Negro Women and the Chicago Women's D ivision of the United Negro College
Fund, as well as a charter member of the Bravo Chapter of the Lyric Opera, the Chicago Chapter of Girl
Friends and the North Shore Chapter of Links, Inc.; and

1884

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 7, 2005

WHEREAS, Hazel Renfroe, subsequent to her retirement, served on advisory committees for African
American Art at the Art Institute of Chicago, the Field Museum and the Chicago Historical Society.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that We, the President and the Board of Commissioners of
Cook County gathered here this June 7, 2005 do hereby offer our hearty congratulations to Hazel Renfroe
on the occasion of her one-hundredth birthday; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a copy of this Resolution be placed in the official proceedings of
this Honorable Body and a suitable copy of same be prepared and presented to Ms. Hazel Renfroe.
Approved and adopted this 7th day of June 2005.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAYID ORR, County Clerk

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved that the Resolution be approved
and adopted. The motion carried unanimously.

05-R-261
RESOLUTION
Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE LARRY SUFFREDIN, CO UNTY COMMISSIONER
Co-Sponsored by
THE HONORABLE JOHN H. STROGER, JR., PRESIDENT, JERRY B UTLER,
FORREST CLAYPOOL, EARLEAN COLLINS, JOHN P. DALEY,
ELI ZABETH ANN DOODY GORMAN, GREGG GOSLIN, CARL R. HANSEN,
ROBERTO MALDONADO, JOSE PH MARIO MORENO, JOAN PATRICIA MURPHY,
ANTHONY J. PERAICA, MIKE Q UIGLEY, PETER N. SILVESTRI, DEBORAH SIMS
AND BOBBIE L. STEELE, COUNTY COMMISSIONERS
IN ME MORY OF HOLLIS SETTLES, JR.
WHEREAS, life-long Evanston resident and community activist Hollis Settles, Jr. passed away on May
18, 2005 at the age of 60; and
WHEREAS, after attending Evanston elementary and secondary schools, Hollis Settles, Jr. earned a
Bachelor of Arts degree from Southern Illinois University; and
WHEREAS, after receiving his diploma, he was employed by Commonwealth Edison as a Human
Resources Representative, a position he held for 30 years; and

1885

 JOURNAL OF PROCEEDINGS FOR JUNE 7, 2005

WHEREAS, believing it was his civic responsibility to be an active participant in the community, Hollis
Settles, Jr. was a lifetime member of the NAACP and served as ! st Vice President of the Evanston Branch
of the NAACP, a position in which he represented the Evanston Branch at regional and state NAACP
events, including training seminars taught by the Civil Rights Advocacy Institute; and
WHEREAS, he additionally served as a member of the Evanston Human Relations Commission and was
appointed by Mayor Lorraine Morton to serve on the Compensation Committee for Elected Officials; and
WHEREAS, a man of seemingly limitless community involvement, he was a member of various local
committees and boards, including the Evanston Community Development Center, the Evanston Cable
Commission, Family Focus Community Forums, the Democratic Party of Evanston, the Evanston
Neighborhood Conference and contributed to the development of the Comm UNITY Picnic, a celebration
of the diversity of Evanston; and
WHEREAS, understanding the importance of educating and mentoring the youth of the community, he
volunteered his time to the Summer Youth Employment Job Fair, where he taught teens the skills
necessary to be successful in the workplace and prepared them for job interviews and after his retirement
from Commonwealth Edison, he worked as a lunchroom supervisor at Haven Middle School in Evanston;
and
WHEREAS, in his most recent mission to improve minority business opportunities, Hollis Settles, Jr.
was able to bring together several minority contractors and businesses to form the Evanston Black
Business Alliance (EBBA), which is working to increase minority participation in Evanston's redevelopment projects; and
WHEREAS, the life of Hollis Settles, Jr. can serve as a inspiration to all citizens of Cook County, for
with his civic participation he has improved the community in which he lived.
NOW, THEREFORE, BE IT RESOLVED, that the Cook County Board of Commissioners does
hereby offer its deepest condolences and most heartfelt sympathy to the family and many friends of Hollis
Settles, Jr. and joins them in sorrow at this time of loss; and
BE IT FURTHER RESOLVED, that a suitable copy of this Resolution be spread upon the official
proceedings of this Honorable Body and that an official copy of same be tendered to the family of Hollis
Settles, Jr. so that his memory may be so honored and ever cherished.
Approved and adopted this 7th day of June 2005.
JOHN H. STROGER, JR., President
Cook County Board of Commissioners
Attest: DAYID ORR, County Clerk

Commissioner Maldonado, seconded by Commissioner Silvestri, moved that the Resolution be approved
and adopted. The motion carried unanimously.
